    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer14060213955774803100">Stanley, an out of work tech writer, is deeply unsatisfied with the lack of meaning in his life. Of the three places he feels should provide meaning in his life, religion, work and family, only one gives his life purpose: family. In PART ONE his lack of meaning starts to change. Out of desperation to support his family, he takes a short-term contract job on the other side </span>
  <span id="freeText14060213955774803100" style="display:none">Stanley, an out of work tech writer, is deeply unsatisfied with the lack of meaning in his life. Of the three places he feels should provide meaning in his life, religion, work and family, only one gives his life purpose: family. In PART ONE his lack of meaning starts to change. Out of desperation to support his family, he takes a short-term contract job on the other side of the country. He cannot afford to fly so he packs his car for the cross-country journey. The trip gets strange almost immediately when he reluctantly picks up a hitchhiker who transforms Stanley's religious views by answering questions that have kept religion at arm's length.</span>

<div id="review_3096160460" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3096160460" />
    <a title="Guy V. Barnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/107185431-guy-v-barnes"><img alt="Guy V. Barnes" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3096160460?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Guy V. Barnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Guy V. Barnes" href="/user/show/107185431-guy-v-barnes">Guy V. Barnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3096160460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7895594957256687357">Some may find The Infinite Jeff: Part 1 to be a well written buddy road trip book, some may feel it is a christian leaning religious tome, some may think it is a supernatural or science fiction morality tale… and in all those cases, it would be a very entertaining read worthy of one’s time. But there is more, much more to Will Holcomb’s thought provoking book.<br/><br/>This modern day parable was like a gentle, but powerful gut punch to my essence as I, like Stanley, am in the journey to find out just who</span>
  <span id="freeText7895594957256687357" style="display:none">Some may find The Infinite Jeff: Part 1 to be a well written buddy road trip book, some may feel it is a christian leaning religious tome, some may think it is a supernatural or science fiction morality tale… and in all those cases, it would be a very entertaining read worthy of one’s time. But there is more, much more to Will Holcomb’s thought provoking book.<br /><br />This modern day parable was like a gentle, but powerful gut punch to my essence as I, like Stanley, am in the journey to find out just who I am and what the meaning and purpose of my life is in this realm. It is written for human beings of the 21st century in a style that speaks to the complexities of the world we currently live in clear prose, not vague metaphorical phrasing.<br /><br />Those allegorical stories are wonderful for lovers of poetic language for poetic language’s sake, and others who love the challenges of figuring out just what the author is trying to say. However, in this technological age where we are bombarded 24/7 with copious information via every medium possible, most of us ‘common folk’ don’t have the time or energy to wander down a multitude of paths trying to find the message the author is attempting to convey.<br /><br />While there are plenty of concepts and ideas to ponder while reading The Infinite Jeff: Part 1, Will’s writing is efficient, and the dialog between the characters flows naturally and believably, providing a brilliant framework that allows the reader to spend their precious time reading, thinking and exploring their own feelings about those concepts and ideas instead of trying to figure out what the author was trying to communicate.<br /><br />This is now one of the books I keep a supply of to give to family, friends and strangers alongside The Power of Now and The Wisdom of the Enneagram.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7895594957256687357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2060128107" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3317783376750966965">I immediately identified with Stanley as Part I opened with his blog. So I sat back and smugly prepared myself to join him on his journey to explore the great “cosmic fluke” of life. However, as his relationship with Jeff started evolving, I initially found myself thinking, “No he’s not going there, is he??” Just as Stanley was not prepared for Jeff, I wasn’t sure I was either. However, by the end of Part I, I found myself highlighting sentences and contemplating the possibility of Jeff’s missio</span>
  <span id="freeText3317783376750966965" style="display:none">I immediately identified with Stanley as Part I opened with his blog. So I sat back and smugly prepared myself to join him on his journey to explore the great “cosmic fluke” of life. However, as his relationship with Jeff started evolving, I initially found myself thinking, “No he’s not going there, is he??” Just as Stanley was not prepared for Jeff, I wasn’t sure I was either. However, by the end of Part I, I found myself highlighting sentences and contemplating the possibility of Jeff’s mission, “to update an ancient message for modern people.” Although I am looking forward to Part II, I’m also glad this parable comes in “waves” because I'm going to need to catch my breath before the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3317783376750966965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780991631148" href="/book/show/44502085-the-infinite-jeff">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5066773-will-holcomb?shelf=spiritual">spiritual</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5066773-will-holcomb?shelf=spirituality-religion">spirituality-religion</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer657197290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17810717195268696252">One piece of advice given to authors is to write the book you want to read. I just re-read parts 1 & 2 of The Infinite Jeff (TIJ) to get ready to edit parts 3 & 4, and I found myself so caught up in the story that I was not taking notes. So I took the advice to heart and wrote the book I wanted to read. To me, it is very relevant to the transition humankind is in today. TIJ looks into many aspects of religion/spirituality, economics, work life/purpose, family relationships, human nature, etc., a</span>
  <span id="freeText17810717195268696252" style="display:none">One piece of advice given to authors is to write the book you want to read. I just re-read parts 1 &amp; 2 of The Infinite Jeff (TIJ) to get ready to edit parts 3 &amp; 4, and I found myself so caught up in the story that I was not taking notes. So I took the advice to heart and wrote the book I wanted to read. To me, it is very relevant to the transition humankind is in today. TIJ looks into many aspects of religion/spirituality, economics, work life/purpose, family relationships, human nature, etc., and through an interesting story offers some ways to look at problems in an interesting way. So, take the time to read The Infinite Jeff and take a fresh look at the world. </span>

          </span>

A wonderful book that had me underlining certain parts and makes me want to re-read several of the books that Jeff gave as gifts and read those in the reading list that I haven't discovered. A book that is perfect for me at this point of my life and has true meaning while being entertaining at the same time. I immediately jumped into Part 2 and it is equally enthralling. </span>

<div id="review_2843270245" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2843270245" />
    <a title="Lucas Israel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/98037466-lucas-israel"><img alt="Lucas Israel" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2843270245?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucas Israel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucas Israel" href="/user/show/98037466-lucas-israel">Lucas Israel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2843270245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2552316200450623971">What a beautiful adaptation of Christian philosophy from a gnostic and syncretic understanding. If you appreciate moral applications of scripture without the historical and fantastical interpretations, this book is brilliant. It is wonderful to see religion described as a tool for growth- as a means for improving your life experience and not an end in itself. This dialect bridges gaps for people divided on religion and science in an enjoyable story that reads fast and fun. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_696359652" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/696359652" />
    <a title="John Fuex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5001859-john-fuex"><img alt="John Fuex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298076101p2/5001859.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/696359652?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Fuex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Fuex" href="/user/show/5001859-john-fuex">John Fuex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer696359652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9583628767052910082">Stanley is an unemployed tech writer driving cross country on his last dime in hopes of an opportunity that will put him back on his feet. He picks up a mysterious hitchhiker who forces himself to re-evaluate the nature of life and religion. <br/><br/>A well written, and interesting perspective on the nature of religion in the context of the reasoning mind of the modern person. It is not a religious book, per se, but is rich with philosophical inquiry about the relevance of "that old time religion" and it</span>
  <span id="freeText9583628767052910082" style="display:none">Stanley is an unemployed tech writer driving cross country on his last dime in hopes of an opportunity that will put him back on his feet. He picks up a mysterious hitchhiker who forces himself to re-evaluate the nature of life and religion. <br /><br />A well written, and interesting perspective on the nature of religion in the context of the reasoning mind of the modern person. It is not a religious book, per se, but is rich with philosophical inquiry about the relevance of "that old time religion" and its dogma for someone with a healthy dose of skeptical rationalism. The protagonist, a modern day doubting Thomas, begins to unravel the nature of his existence and path through life with the aide of his traveling companion, who is clearly more than meets the eye. <br /><br />Looking forward to parts 2 and 3, which I hear are nearing completion. A fine first effort by Will Holcomb.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9583628767052910082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1503828814352170748" style="display:none">This book was refereed to me by a friend and was pleased when the pages stated to fly by. One of the main characters was clearly a real person and some one I could relate too. Stanley and I share many of the the same personally traits (sorry Stanley) so it was easy follow. Jeff (also main character) crazy man or super hero? Who knows you decide. He has something for everyone. Stanley and Jeff's journey across the country explores the questions we ask every day about faith and love and can you take a punch. The answers may not be what your were expecting. The story line invaded my thoughts when not reading the words. Decisions are made between my ears every day and I wonder Vertical or Horizontal growth? Thanks Jeff! Read the story you will understand.</span>

<div id="review_1191220833" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1191220833" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1191220833?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary Roland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary Roland" href="/user/show/39951904-mary-roland">Mary Roland</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1191220833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9218299407126748041">The thing about this book is that many people will relate to Stanley's plight in having been laid off and getting desperate to find work to pay the bills. The adventure of his life and maybe our own is when he opens himself up to Jeff, a stranger, who rides along with Stanley on a cross-country trek to a new job. Jeff's unique perspectives on life, truth, humanity and love transform Stanley and begin to set him free from the defensive barriers he's built around himself and readers will find them</span>
  <span id="freeText9218299407126748041" style="display:none">The thing about this book is that many people will relate to Stanley's plight in having been laid off and getting desperate to find work to pay the bills. The adventure of his life and maybe our own is when he opens himself up to Jeff, a stranger, who rides along with Stanley on a cross-country trek to a new job. Jeff's unique perspectives on life, truth, humanity and love transform Stanley and begin to set him free from the defensive barriers he's built around himself and readers will find themselves examining their own as well. I know I did and I can't wait to read the rest of Stanley's adventures when the final parts are released, too.<br /><br />This is well-crafted and thought provoking. It would be a good book club selection, too, because it will instantly start discussion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9218299407126748041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              >

This mysterious mentor story reminds me a bit of the Donald Shimoda character from Richard Bach's book Illusions. Maybe upon reading Infinite Jeff, you'll find your mentor in the next stranger you meet.</span>

          </span>

<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_67896'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/67896.Tao_Te_Ching"><img alt="Tao Te Ching" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1333578861l/67896._SX98_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LDUshci0VYAJGX+hzG74kpWKo43n7cfEnE120JlZ0WnyY9LeYNXh+10p3YT+fSSt/pcO9mvLi3Q8Q8bvHCD3Qw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WCUiEMwda/nyhxkeCddkDCfPrQDhDJTyIerf7Bkt05OGc9xLZHzfgqa3uzs7xLgzTNIAe20q2EKB5G/TnFT1uQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

And while this message may not seem stunningly original or fresh, Tolle\'s clear writing, supportive voice and enthusiasm make this an excellent manual for anyone who\'s ever wondered what exactly &quot;living in the now&quot; means. Foremost, Tolle is a world-class teacher, able to explain complicated concepts in concrete language. More importantly, within a chapter of reading this book, readers are already holding the world in a different container--more conscious of how thoughts and emotions get in the way of their ability to live in genuine peace and happiness.Tolle packs a lot of information and inspirational ideas into The Power of Now. (Topics include the source of Chi, enlightened relationships, creative use of the mind, impermanence and the cycle of life.) Thankfully, he\'s added markers that symbolise &quot;break time&quot;. This is when readers should close the book and mull over what they just read. As a result, The Power of Now reads like the highly acclaimed A Course in Miracles--a spiritual guidebook that has the potential to inspire just as many study groups and change just as many lives for <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13917490542369660597">Will Holcomb is a software engineer, writer and playwright, among other things. His four part book <i>The Infinite Jeff, </i> explores questions facing both the individual and society/humanity. It takes a fascinating look at religion and human potential. He is currently editing part 4 of <i>The Infinite Jeff, </i> and working on a new play. His first play,<i>Shakespeare Rocks</i>, was written for a youth troupe as a f</span>
  <span id="freeText13917490542369660597" style="display:none">Will Holcomb is a software engineer, writer and playwright, among other things. His four part book <i>The Infinite Jeff, </i> explores questions facing both the individual and society/humanity. It takes a fascinating look at religion and human potential. He is currently editing part 4 of <i>The Infinite Jeff, </i> and working on a new play. His first play,<i>Shakespeare Rocks</i>, was written for a youth troupe as a fun way to get them interested in Shakespeare. His second play, <i>Clinically Un-Depressed</i>, premiered to sold out shows and standing ovations. It was the highest grossing show for Bastrop Opera House's 2017/2018 season. It explores the possibility of how lives could be transformed if we simply reacted differently to others. <br /><br />Follow him on Facebook: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/willholcombauthor/">https://www.facebook.com/willholcomba...</a></span>
